## Your Task

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)

  1016→        allMembers().stream().map(member -> member.vote(candidates))
  1017→            .forEach(protocolName -> {
  1018→                int count = votesByProtocol.getOrDefault(protocolName, 0);

   850→        if (subscribedRegularExpressions.isEmpty()) {
   851→            // If the members do not use regular expressions, the subscription is
   852→            // considered as homogeneous if all the members are subscribed to the
   853→            // same topics. Otherwise, it is considered as heterogeneous.
   854→            for (SubscriptionCount subscriberCount : subscribedTopicNames.values()) {
   855→                if (subscriberCount.byNameCount != numberOfMembers) {
   856→                    return HETEROGENEOUS;
   857→                }
   858→            }
   859→            return HOMOGENEOUS;
   860→        } else {
   861→            int count = subscribedRegularExpressions.values().iterator().next();
   862→            if (count == numberOfMembers) {
   863→                // If all the members are subscribed to a single regular expressions
   864→                // and none of them are subscribed to topic names, the subscription
   865→                // is considered as homogeneous. If some members are subscribed to
   866→                // topic names too, the subscription is considered as heterogeneous.
   867→                for (SubscriptionCount subscriberCount : subscribedTopicNames.values()) {
   868→                    if (subscriberCount.byRegexCount != 1 || subscriberCount.byNameCount > 0) {
   869→                        return HETEROGENEOUS;
   870→                    }
   871→                }
   872→                return HOMOGENEOUS;
   873→            } else {
   874→                // The subscription is considered as heterogeneous because
   875→                // there is a mix of regular expressions.
   876→                return SubscriptionType.HETEROGENEOUS;
   877→            }
   878→        }

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about the Kafka consumer group coordinator's state machine implementation.

## Summary

I found **22 Java source files** in apache/kafka that implement the consumer group coordinator's state machine. The implementation is organized by group type:

### Classic Group State Machine
- **ClassicGroupState.java** - Defines the 5-state enum (EMPTY, PREPARING_REBALANCE, COMPLETING_REBALANCE, STABLE, DEAD)
- **ClassicGroup.java** - Contains `transitionTo()` method for state transitions
- **ClassicGroupMember.java** - Manages member-level state

### Modern Consumer Group State Machine  
- **ConsumerGroup.java** - Epoch-based states (EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD) with `maybeUpdateGroupState()`
- **ConsumerGroupMember.java** - Member reconciliation tracking
- **CurrentAssignmentBuilder.java** - Reconciliation engine managing member state convergence

### Streams & Share Group State Machines
- **StreamsGroup.java** - 6-state machine with NOT_READY state for task-based groups
- **ShareGroup.java** - Simplified state model
- Their respective member and assignment builder classes

### Core Coordination
- **GroupMetadataManager.java** - Central orchestrator driving Join/Sync protocol phases
- **GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers.java** - Persistence of state transitions

The answer includes all file paths, key symbols (classes and methods), and a detailed narrative explaining how Join, Sync, and Rebalance protocol phases are implemented across all group types.

state machine is implemented across multiple Java files in the apache/kafka repository, organized by group type (classic, modern consumer, share, and streams). The core implementation consists of 22 files that manage Join, Sync, and Rebalance states and their transitions.\\n\\nClassic Group State Machine (apache/kafka/group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/):\\nThe classic group coordinator implements a 5-state machine defined in ClassicGroupState.java with states: EMPTY, PREPARING_REBALANCE, COMPLETING_REBALANCE, STABLE, and DEAD. The ClassicGroup.java file contains the transitionTo() method which orchestrates state transitions in response to JoinGroup (triggering EMPTY \u2192 PREPARING_REBALANCE), timeout (PREPARING_REBALANCE \u2192 COMPLETING_REBALANCE), SyncGroup (COMPLETING_REBALANCE \u2192 STABLE), and various failure scenarios. ClassicGroupMember.java manages individual member state within these rebalance phases.\\n\\nModern Consumer Group State Machine (apache/kafka/group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/):\\nConsumerGroup.java implements a consumer group state machine with states: EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, and DEAD. Unlike classic groups, the consumer protocol uses epoch-based state transitions. The maybeUpdateGroupState() method triggers transitions between ASSIGNING and RECONCILING states as members reconcile their assignments. The CurrentAssignmentBuilder.java implements the reconciliation engine that manages the convergence of current and target assignment states at the member level, tracking STABLE, UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS, UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS states during rebalance.\\n\\nShare Group State Machine (apache/kafka/group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/share/):\\nShareGroup.java provides a simplified state model with EMPTY, STABLE, DEAD, and UNKNOWN states. ShareGroupAssignmentBuilder.java manages assignment reconciliation similar to the consumer group protocol.\\n\\nStreams Group State Machine (apache/kafka/group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/streams/):\\nStreamsGroup.java implements the most complex state model with states: EMPTY, NOT_READY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, and DEAD. StreamsGroupMember.java and CurrentAssignmentBuilder.java manage task-based assignment reconciliation using StreamsGroupHeartbeatResult.java for state change tracking.\\n\\nCentral Orchestration (apache/kafka/group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/):\\nGroupMetadataManager.java serves as the central coordinator that orchestrates all state machines. It implements the actual JoinGroup and SyncGroup handler methods that drive the Join and Sync phases of the rebalance protocol. The GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers.java and StreamsCoordinatorRecordHelpers.java files manage the persistence of state transitions through log records.\\n\\nThe state machines implement the Kafka group rebalance protocol where: (1) Join phase accepts new members and transitions to a join-wait state, (2) Sync phase collects assignments from the leader and distributes them to followers triggering state reconciliation, and (3) Rebalance transitions handle member failures, new subscriptions, and generation advances that restart the join and sync phases.\"\n}\n",
